## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and external driving. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or coupling terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically forced linear oscillator)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (polynomial potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (x**2 + v**2) (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (quintic Duffing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric potential wells (Duffing-type); even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity terms proportional to v indicate linear dissipation; terms like v*x**2 indicate amplitude-dependent (Van der Pol-type) nonlinear damping
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative with a potential energy function derivable by integration
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v) can indicate velocity-dependent forces arising from magnetic or Coriolis-like interactions
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with cubic velocity saturation indicates self-sustained oscillation (limit cycle behavior)
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions suggests the system is non-autonomous but periodically driven, not explicitly time-varying
- Sign of the cubic term coefficient determines hardening (same sign as linear) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0857*v³ - 1.9196*v - 1.7303*x*(0.0808*t + 1) + 0.7193*sin(t)`

Expanding: `-0.0857*v³ - 1.9196*v - 1.7303*x - 0.1398*t*x + 0.7193*sin(t)`

The GT has these terms:
1. A constant × v³
2. A constant × v
3. A constant × x
4. A constant × t·x
5. A constant × sin(t)

The sin(t) term can be written as `exp(0*t)*sin(1*t + 0)`, so candidates with `exp(c*t)*sin(c*t + c)` can match by setting the exp coefficient to 0 and frequency to 1.

Let me check candidates that have: v³, v, x, t·x (or equivalent), and sin(t) terms, without requiring extra terms that can't be zeroed.

**Candidate 15:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*t*x + c3*exp(c4*t)*sin(c5*t + c6) + c7*v + c8*v³ + x⁴`

This has: x, x³, t·x, exp·sin, v, v³, and a fixed x⁴ term. The x⁴ term has coefficient 1 and cannot be zeroed. Setting c1=0 removes x³, but x⁴ remains. **No match.**

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x + c1*exp(c2*t)*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*x*(c8 + t)^c9`

The last term: `c7*x*(c8 + t)^c9`. If c9=1: `c7*x*(c8 + t) = c7*c8*x + c7*t*x`. This gives both x and t·x terms. Combined with c0*x, we get: `(c0 + c7*c8)*x + c7*t*x`. 

Setting c2=0: `c1*sin(c3*t + c4)`. Need c3=1, c4=0 to get sin(t).

So candidate 5 becomes: `(c0 + c7*c8)*x + c1*sin(t) + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*t*x`

This matches the GT structure perfectly!
- c6 = -0.0857 (for v³)
- c5 = -1.9196 (for v)
- c7 = -0.1398 (for t·x), then c0 + c7*c8 = -1.7303
- c1 = 0.7193 (for sin(t))
- c2 = 0, c3 = 1, c4 = 0

Let me verify: c7*c8 = -1.7303 - c0. We can choose c0 and c8 freely. For example, c0=0, c8 = -1.7303/(-0.1398) ≈ 12.375. ✓

**Candidate 5 matches!**

Let me also quickly check **Candidate 9:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*t*x + c3*exp(c4*t)*sin(c5*t + c6) + c7*v + c8*x⁵ + c9*x + x⁴`

Has fixed x⁴ term. **No match.**

**Candidate 41:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*v + c7*x*(c8 + t)^c9 + x⁴`

Has fixed x⁴. **No match** unless... no, can't zero x⁴.

Candidate 5 is confirmed as a match.
